## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position, velocity, and time. The acceleration in such systems typically involves restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and possibly driving forces (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Cubic nonlinear restoring force (Duffing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (Duffing oscillator restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping, van der Pol type)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - x**2) * v + c1 * x (nonlinear damping with restoring force)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Driven nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (Duffing with periodic driving)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Cubic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity-dependent friction)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Mixed nonlinear terms: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 (combined Duffing and van der Pol)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent stiffness)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) â†’ symmetric potential wells, preserving oscillator symmetry
- Terms proportional to (1 - x**2)*v â†’ self-sustained oscillations with amplitude-limiting (limit cycles)
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) â†’ external periodic driving force
- Velocity-position coupling v*x^n â†’ nonlinear damping that depends on oscillation amplitude
- Pure odd-function dependence on x â†’ symmetric oscillation about equilibrium (no drift)
- Even-power position terms (x**2) in restoring force â†’ broken symmetry, asymmetric oscillation
- Negative linear damping (positive coefficient of v) combined with cubic velocity term â†’ self-excited oscillations with saturation
- Product of position and time-periodic function x*cos(c*t) â†’ parametric resonance phenomena
